Navigating the Logical Collection
Title page listing contents of a printed logical collection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main text, its commentary, and supplementary works from a title page of an Islamic logical collection.

Core Idea
A single title page reveals the entire logical curriculum and its scholarly lineage.

This lesson introduces the front matter of a printed collection of logical works. The title page is not merely decorative; it is a roadmap that tells you which texts are included, who authored them, and how they relate to each other. Understanding this structure helps you situate the primary text—Tadhheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam—within a tradition of commentary and gloss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central work
Find the base text that is the focus of the collection. Here it is 'Tadhheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam' by al-Taftazani (spelled as al-Shiftazani in the text). This is a foundational work in logic and theology.
The author's name may appear with variant spellings due to OCR.
2
Locate its primary commentary
Look for a direct commentary on the central work. The phrase 'على تهذيب المنطق والكلام' indicates that 'Al-Talmi'a al-Laqis' is a commentary on Tadhheeb.
The commentary title 'Al-Talmi'a al-Laqis' is uncommon; it may be a gloss or supercommentary.
3
Note supplementary works
The title page also lists 'Al-Tajreed al-Shafi on Tadhheeb al-Kafi', which is a separate commentary on a related text. This shows the collection includes multiple layers of logical writings.
Tadhheeb al-Kafi is another logical work by al-Dusuqi.
4
Recognize glossators and editors
Additional names like Hasan al-Attar (gloss) and Abd al-Jayyid al-Sharnubi (marginalia) indicate further scholarly contributions. The final line credits modern editors and the publishing house.
These names help trace the transmission and editorial history of the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجموعة المنطقية وتحتوي على التلمية اللقيص على تهذيب المنطق والكلام للشفتازاني وعليه ما شتان التجريد الشافي على تهذيب الكافي للملامة محمد بن عرفة الدسوقي وحاشية العلامة حسن العطار وهوامش للشيخ عبد الجيد الشرنوبي رحمهم الله جميعا الشيخ خالد خليل الراهدي الشيخ عبد الكرتير كاني سيفي اعتنى به مركز أمير لتحقيق المخطوطات في كركوك دار ابن حزم كركوك العراق
The Logical Collection. It contains: Al-Talmi'a al-Laqis on Tadhheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam by al-Shiftazani; and upon it (as gloss?) 'Ma Shatta'? Al-Tajreed al-Shafi on Tadhheeb al-Kafi by al-Mullama Muhammad bin Arafa al-Dusuqi; and the gloss of al-Allama Hasan al-Attar; and marginalia by Sheikh Abd al-Jayyid al-Sharnubi. May Allah have mercy on them all. Sheikh Khalid Khalil al-Rahidi, Sheikh Abd al-Kurter Kani Sayfi. Cared for by: Markaz Amir li-Tahqeeq al-Makhtutat in Kirkuk. Dar Ibn Hazm, Kirkuk, Iraq.
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage is a title page from a printed collection of logical works. It lists the main works included: first, 'Al-Talmi'a al-Laqis' which is a commentary (probably a gloss or supercommentary) on 'Tadhheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam' by al-Shiftazani (likely a misspelling of al-Taftazani). Then it mentions 'Ma Shatta' (possibly a separate work or gloss), then 'Al-Tajreed al-Shafi' on 'Tadhheeb al-Kafi' by Muhammad bin Arafa al-Dusuqi. It also includes a gloss by Hasan al-Attar and marginalia by Abd al-Jayyid al-Sharnubi. The page ends with the names of two scholars (Khalid al-Rahidi and Abd al-Kurter Kani Sayfi) and indicates that the edition was prepared by Markaz Amir li-Tahqeeq al-Makhtutat in Kirkuk, published by Dar Ibn Hazm. This is purely bibliographic information, setting the stage for the logical texts to follow.

Key Takeaway
The title page of a logical collection provides a structured overview of the main work, its commentaries, and the scholarly chain, enabling proper orientation for study.

Introduction and Front Matter

Parsing the Title Page: Layers of a Commentary Volume
Front matter listing the volume's contents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse a classical Islamic book title page to identify the base text, the main commentary, glosses, and marginal notes, and understand the scholarly chain of transmission.

Core Idea
A single volume often contains multiple layers of scholarship — base, commentary, gloss, and marginal notes.

This lesson examines a title page from a widely used logic textbook. The page tells us not only the name of the book but also the entire scholarly tradition surrounding it. By learning to read such pages, you gain insight into how Islamic scholars built upon each other's work over centuries. Let's break down the components.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text (matn)
Look for the core work that is being commented upon. Here it is 'Tahdheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam' by al-Taftazani.
2
Identify the main commentary (sharh)
The work that explains the base text. Here it is 'al-Tadhheeb al-Himsi'.
3
Identify the glosses (hashiyat)
Super-commentaries on the main commentary. Here there are two: by al-Dusuqi and al-'Attar.
4
Identify marginal notes (hawamish)
Additional notes by a later scholar. Here by al-Sharnubi.
5
Note editorial and publication details
The names of those who read and corrected the text, and the publisher. This shows the scholarly chain involved in producing the edition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المجموعة المنطقية وتحتوي على عربي التذهيب الحمصي على تهذيب المنطق والكلام للتفتازاني وعليه حاشيتان التجريد الشافي على تذهيب الكافي للعلامة محمد بن عرفة الدسوقي وحاشية العلامة حسن العطار وهوامش للشيخ عبد المجيد الشرنوبي رحمهم الله جميعا قراه وضبطه الشيخ خالد خليل الزاهدي والشيخ عبد الكريم كاني سيفي اعتنى به مركز أمير لتحقيق المخطوطات في كركوك دار ابن حزم كركوك العراق
The Logical Collection, containing the Arabic Tadhheeb al-Himsi on Tahdheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam of al-Taftazani, and upon it two glosses: al-Tajreed al-Shafi 'ala Tadhheeb al-Kafi by the scholar Muhammad ibn 'Arafa al-Dusuqi, and the gloss of the scholar Hasan al-'Attar, and marginal notes by Shaykh 'Abd al-Majid al-Sharnubi, may God have mercy on them all. Read and corrected by Shaykh Khalid Khalil al-Zahidi and Shaykh 'Abd al-Karim Kani Sayfi. Supervised by the Center of Amir for Manuscript Editing in Kirkuk. Dar Ibn Hazm, Kirkuk, Iraq.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the book, specifically the title page that describes the contents of the volume. It identifies the main work as 'al-Tadhheeb al-Himsi', which is a commentary on 'Tahdheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam' by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. The volume also includes two important glosses (hashiyas): the first is 'al-Tajreed al-Shafi' by Muhammad ibn 'Arafa al-Dusuqi, and the second is by Hasan al-'Attar. Additionally, there are marginal notes (hawamish) by 'Abd al-Majid al-Sharnubi. The passage then notes that the book was read and corrected (qarāhu wa ḍabaṭahu) by two contemporary scholars, Khalid Khalil al-Zahidi and 'Abd al-Karim Kani Sayfi, and that the editing was supervised by the Center of Amir for Manuscript Editing in Kirkuk. Finally, the publisher is Dar Ibn Hazm, located in Kirkuk and Beirut. This information is crucial for understanding the provenance and scholarly chain of the text.

تهذيب المنطق والكلام
حاشية

A title page is not just a label—it is a map of the scholarly tradition, showing the base text and all subsequent commentary layers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Navigating the Title Page of a Classical Logic Text
Front matter listing the book and its two glosses and editors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main text, its two glosses, and the editors of a classical logic collection from its title page.

Core Idea
A title page is a map to the text's lineage.

When you open a classical Islamic logic text, the title page is not mere decoration. It tells you which text is primary, which commentaries and glosses accompany it, and who edited the edition. This lesson teaches you how to read that bibliographic information so you can situate the work in its scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the main text title
The title page begins with the main work. Look for the phrase 'على تهذيب المنطق والكلام' which indicates the base text by al-Taftazani, while the headline is the commentary.
In this collection, the main text is 'التذهيب الحمصي' (al-Tadhheeb al-Himsi), a commentary on al-Taftazani's Tahdheeb.
2
Identify the two glosses (حاشيتان)
After the main text, the phrase 'وعليه حاشيتان' introduces two super-commentaries. Note their titles and authors: 'التجريد الشافي' by al-Dusuqi and another by al-Attar.
These glosses are secondary commentaries that explain or critique the primary commentary.
3
Note marginal notes and editors
The page lists additional 'هوامش' (marginal notes) by al-Sharnubi and the scholars who read and corrected the edition (al-Zahidi and al-Sayfi). This is part of the manuscript's transmission history.
The editors' names and the publishing center (Amir Center for Manuscript Research) help verify the edition's reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المجموعة المنطق وتحتوي على عربي التذهيب الحمصي على تهذيب المنطق والكلام للتفتازاني وعليه حاشيتان التجريد الشافي على تذهيب الكافي للعلامة محمد بن عرفة الدسوقي وحاشية العلامة حسن العطار وهوامش للشيخ عبد الجيد الشرنوبي مهم الله جميعا قراه وضبطه الشيخ خالد خليل الزاهدي الشيخ عبد الكريم كاني سيفي اعتنى به مركز أمير لتحقيق المخطوطات في كركوك دار ابن حزم كركوك - العراق
The logic collection contains Arabic: al-Tadhheeb al-Himsi on the Tahdheeb of Logic and Kalam of al-Taftazani, and upon it two glosses: al-Tajrid al-Shafi on Tadhheeb al-Kafi by the scholar Muhammad bin Arafa al-Dusuqi, and the gloss of the scholar Hasan al-Attar, and marginal notes of the teacher Abd al-Jayyid al-Sharnubi. May Allah benefit all. Read and corrected by Sheikh Khalid Khalil al-Zahidi and Sheikh Abd al-Karim Kani Sayfi. Edited by the Amir Center for Manuscript Research in Kirkuk, Dar ibn Hazm, Kirkuk - Iraq.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a title page of a printed collection of logic works. It identifies the main text as 'al-Tadhheeb al-Himsi' which is a commentary (or perhaps a super-commentary) on the classic 'Tahdheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam' by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. The page then lists two glosses (hawashi) that are included: 'al-Tajrid al-Shafi' by Muhammad bin Arafa al-Dusuqi, and a gloss by Hasan al-Attar. Additionally, there are marginal notes (hawamish) by Abd al-Jayyid al-Sharnubi. The work was read and corrected by two scholars, Khalid Khalil al-Zahidi and Abd al-Karim Kani Sayfi, and published by the Amir Center for Manuscript Research in Kirkuk, Iraq, through Dar ibn Hazm. This provides essential bibliographic context for the student: the main text, its commentators, and the editorial history.

Introduction and Front Matter

Understanding the Sharh-Hashiya Tradition: Al-Khubaysi's Commentary on al-Tahdhib
Describes the importance of al-Khubaysi's commentary and its supercommentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three famous commentaries on al-Tahdhib and explain how supercommentaries (hawashi) build on base commentaries.

Core Idea
Commentaries and supercommentaries form an intellectual chain that transmits and refines knowledge across generations.

This preface introduces al-Khubaysi's commentary on al-Taftazani's al-Tahdhib, a foundational text in logic and theology. The author explains why this commentary became a curriculum standard and lists the other major commentaries and their glosses. Understanding this chain of commentary helps you trace how ideas develop in the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and its subject
Find that al-Tahdhib is by al-Taftazani and covers both logic (mantiq) and theology (kalam). Note that the author mentions this text is the matn for the commentaries.
The base text is the foundation; knowing its scope helps understand what later scholars engaged with.
2
Distinguish between the two parts of al-Tahdhib
The author observes that the logical part (the first) gained wide acceptance and many commentaries, while the theological part (the second) remained obscure. This highlights how scholarly attention can be uneven.
This distinction is important for understanding the focus of later works.
3
List the three famous commentaries on Tahdhib al-Mantiq
The passage names three: by al-Jalal al-Dawwani, Abdullah al-Yazawi, and Fakhr al-Din al-Khubaysi (the subject of this edition). Note that al-Khubaysi titled his work al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahdhib.
Remember these names as key figures in the logical tradition.
4
Understand the role of supercommentaries (hawashi)
Each commentary attracted many hawashi (glosses) and taqrirat (critical notes). The author highlights al-Dasuki's gloss as the most important, followed by al-Attar's. These supercommentaries further explain and critique the commentary.
Supercommentaries represent the next layer of scholarly refinement.
5
Appreciate the printing history and its significance
The author laments that al-Dasuki's gloss has not been printed in a good modern edition; most prints are old lithographs. This explains why a new edition is needed and shows the practical challenges of accessing classical texts.
Understanding publication history helps assess the reliability of available editions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والراسخون في عالم الكتب يعلمون أن شرح الخبيصي من يوم ولادته وبزوغ نور فجره أصبح محل نظر العلماء، ومقصد طلبة العلم النجباء، يدرسونه ويتدارسونه، ويدورون في فلك فرائده ويقتنصون شوارد فوائده. ولا عجب فهو من المقررات المنهجية التي يتخرج عليها العلماء في الأزهر الشريف، وغيره من المحافل العلمية، ومركز الدراسات الشرعية في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها، فهو مطلوب لدى طلاب العلم الشرعي والوسط العلمي، وهو من أهم كتب المنطق التي تعد مصدراً قيماً من مصادر هذا العلم. ومن أواخر الفحول الذين درسوا الكتاب أستاذنا العلامة المحقق الأصولي الدكتور محمد سالم أبو عاصي. وأصل الشرح متن متين للعلامة سعد الدين التفتازاني في علمي المنطق والكلام أسماه (التهذيب)، رزق الأول القبول فكثر شارحوه، وأصاب الثاني الخمول فقل ذاكروه، والله سبحانه في خلقه شؤون. أشهر شروح (تهذيب المنطق) ثلاثة: شرح العلامة الجلال الديواني، والمحقق عبد الله اليزوي، وشرح العلامة الذي نحن في خدمته الإمام فخر الدين الخبيصي، وأسماه (التذهيب في شرح التهذيب)، وكل واحد من هذه الشروح كثر عليها الحواشي والتقريرات، وكان نصيب (التهذيب) منها ستة، وكان من أهمها وواسطة عقدها ودرة تاجها حاشية العلامة الدسوقي رحمه الله تعالى وتبعها حاشية العلامة العطار. ولكن ما يحز في النفس أن هذه الحاشية - على نفاستها - لم تطبع طباعة معاصرة جيدة وأغلب إصداراتها الحديثة هي تصوير عن طبعاتها القديمة، وقد طبعت هذه الحاشية طبعة حجرية قديمة قبل أكثر من مئة وثلاثة عشر عاماً في مطبعة
The deeply rooted in the world of books know that al-Khubaysi's commentary from the day of its birth and the dawn of its light became a subject of scholars' scrutiny and the goal of the elite students of knowledge; they study it and study it together, and revolve in the orbit of its unique gems and hunt its scattered benefits. No wonder, for it is among the methodological curricula upon which scholars graduate in al-Azhar al-Sharif and other academic assemblies and the center of Islamic studies in the East and West of the earth; it is sought by students of Islamic knowledge and the academic community, and it is among the most important books of logic that are considered a valuable source of this science. Among the latest eminent figures who studied the book is our professor, the accomplished fundamentalist scholar Dr. Muhammad Salim Abu Asi. The origin of the commentary is a solid text by the scholar Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani in the two sciences of logic and theology, which he named al-Tahdhib; the first (i.e., the commentary) received acceptance, so its commentators multiplied, and the second (i.e., the text on theology) received neglect, so its discussants became few, and Allah Almighty has affairs in His creation. The most famous commentaries on Tahdhib al-Mantiq are three: the commentary by al-Jalal al-Dawwani, that of the investigator Abdullah al-Yazawi, and the commentary of the scholar whom we are serving, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Khubaysi, which he named al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahdhib. Each one of these commentaries had many supercommentaries and critical notes, and al-Tahdhib's share of them was six, and among the most important of them, the central gem and the pearl of its crown, is the gloss of al-Dasuki — may Allah have mercy on him — followed by the gloss of al-Attar. But what grieves the soul is that this gloss — despite its value — has not been printed in a good contemporary edition, and most of its modern publications are photographic reproductions of its old prints. This gloss was printed in a lithographic edition more than one hundred and thirteen years ago in a printing press.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the preface of the editor, introducing the book and its background. It begins by praising al-Khubaysi's commentary on Tahdhib al-Mantiq, stating that from its inception it became a central text for scholars and students, studied and discussed extensively. The author then explains that this commentary is part of the curriculum at al-Azhar and other Islamic institutions, making it essential for students of Islamic law and the academic community. He mentions that one of the latest scholars to study this book is Dr. Muhammad Salim Abu Asi. The passage then provides the origin: the base text (matn) is Tahdhib al-Mantiq by al-Taftazani, which covers both logic and theology. Interestingly, the author notes that the logical part (the first) gained wide acceptance and many commentaries, while the theological part (the second) remained obscure. He then lists the three most famous commentaries on Tahdhib: those of al-Dawwani, al-Yazawi, and al-Khubaysi (the one at hand, titled al-Tadhheeb). On each of these, many supercommentaries (hawashi) and critical notes (taqrirat) were written, and al-Tahdhib alone has six such works. Among them, the most important is the gloss (hashiya) of al-Dasuki, followed by that of al-Attar. Finally, the author laments that despite its value, al-Dasuki's gloss has not been published in a good modern edition; most current prints are reproductions of old lithographs, the last being over 113 years ago. This sets the stage for the edition being presented.

Key Terms
التهذيب (al-Tahdhib): The work by al-Taftazani on logic and theology that is the base text for the commentaries discussed. [Note: No significant shift; refers to this specific work by al-Taftazani.]
التذهيب في شرح التهذيب (al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahdhib): The commentary on al-Tahdhib by al-Khubaysi, which is the main subject of the preface. [Note: Distinct from other commentaries with similar names.]
الحاشية (al-hashiya): A supercommentary or gloss on a commentary, specifically here referring to al-Dasuki's gloss on al-Khubaysi's commentary. [Note: Standard usage across the tradition.]
الشرح (al-sharh): Commentary; here referring to the three main commentaries on al-Tahdhib. [Note: Stable term.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many most famous commentaries on Tahdhib al-Mantiq does the author mention?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The commentary tradition is a living chain of scholarship; understanding its layers is essential for accessing classical Islamic texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a similar commentary chain in another Islamic science, such as tafsir or hadith. Name the base text, its commentary, and one supercommentary. Explain how each layer adds value.
?
Using the information from this passage, create a diagram showing the relationship between al-Taftazani's al-Tahdhib, the three commentaries, and the supercommentaries of al-Dasuki and al-Attar.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Textual Lineage of Islamic Logic: Matn, Sharh, Hashiya
Introduces the textual tradition of al-Tahzeeb and its commentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three layers of a classical Islamic logical work (matn, sharh, hashiya) and trace the lineage of al-Tahzeeb, al-Tadhheeb, and al-Dasuqi's hashiya.

Core Idea
Islamic learning is built on layers of commentary that preserve and refine core texts.

This passage is the editor's introduction to a new edition of al-Dasuqi's gloss. It provides a rare window into how the tradition of logic was transmitted through a chain of texts: the original matn, its most famous commentary, and the super-commentaries that followed. Understanding this chain is essential for any student of Islamic logic, as it determines which texts are authoritative and how knowledge is preserved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text (matn)
Look for the name of the original work and its author. The passage mentions 'al-Tahzeeb' by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. This is the core text on logic and kalam.
The matn is the foundation upon which all later works are built.
2
Identify the commentary (sharh)
Find the commentary on the matn. Here, al-Khabisi's 'al-Tadhheeb' is the commentary. The passage lists it among the three most famous commentaries on al-Tahzeeb.
The sharh explains and expands the matn.
3
Identify the super-commentary (hashiyah)
Locate the gloss upon the commentary. The editor focuses on al-Dasuqi's hashiyah, which is a super-commentary on al-Khabisi's sharh. It is called a 'hashiyah' and is considered the most important of its kind.
Hashiyahs often engage critically with the sharh, refining or correcting points.
4
Understand the editorial work
The author explains why a new edition was needed: the old lithographic print had errors, missing text, and lacked proper punctuation. This shows the importance of textual criticism in Islamic scholarship.
Not all editions are reliable; critical editions are vital for accurate study.

والراسخون في عالم الكتب يعلمون أن شرح الخبيصي من يوم ولادته وبزوغ نور فجره أصبح محل نظر العلماء، ومقصد طلبة العلم النجباء، يدرسونه ويتدارسونه، ويدورون في فلك فرائده ويقتنصون شوارد فوائده. ولا عجب فهو اليزوي، وشرح العلامة الذي نحن في خدمته الإمام فخر الدين الخبيصي، وأسماه التذهيب في شرح التهذيب، وكل واحد من هذه الشروح كثر عليها الحواشي والتقريرات، وكان نصيب التهذيب منها ستة، وكان من أهمها وواسطة عقدها ودرة تاجها، حاشية العلامة الدسوقي رحمه الله تعالى وتبعها حاشية العلامة العطار. ولكن ما يحز في النفس أن هذه الحاشية على نفاستها لم تطبع طباعة معاصرة جيدة وأغلب إصداراتها الحديثة هي تصوير عن طبعاتها القديمة، وقد طبعت هذه الحاشية طبعة حجرية قديمة قبل أكثر من مئة وثلاثة عشر عاما في مطبعة كردستان العلمية بالقاهرة، المعروفة بإتقانها وصحة طبعتها، وذلك سنة 1328هـ إلا أنها كانت تفتقد الكثير من الضبط، فقد وجد فيها سقط لكثير من الكلمات والعبارات، والأخطاء والتحريف وذلك بعد مقابلتها بالمخطوط، وكان ينقصها علامات الترقيم والترتيب لمباحثها وهذا مما يعاني منه طلبة العلم أثناء قراءتهم لها على شيوخهم، ولو أنها خالية صحيحة سليمة لما قمنا بهذا العمل الجليل الذي يهدف إلى خدمة طلبة العلم. فشمّرنا عن ساعد الجد بفضل الله تعالى، ثم بتشجيع من الأخ العزيز الكتبي العراقي المشهور الأستاذ أمير العثماني صاحب مكتبة أمير للنشر والتوزيع ومركز أمير لتحقيق المخطوطات في كركوك الذي دعمتي بإنجاز هذا السفر النفيس وزودني بالمخطوطات واعتنى به قراءة وتدقيقا وترتيبا وضبطا وتصحيحا لنصوصها، وإخراجا على الحلة التي ترونها؛ حرصا منه على خدمة العلم وأهله. وختاما أشكر الشيخ عبد الكريم كاني سيفي مدرّس في بيارة الشريفة السليمانية على ما قدمه من العون في مراجعة الحاشية، وتصحيح بعض المصطلحات التي تحتاج إلى أهل الاختصاص، فكان أهلا لها، فجزاه الله عنا كل خير. وأشكر كل أخ كريم وجد خطأ، أو خللا، أو نقصا، فراسلنا لتداركه في طبعته الثانية إن شاء الله تعالى فالإنسان محل للسهو والنسيان والمرء قليل بنفسه كثير بإخوانه، وبعضنا يكمل الآخر، وجزاكم الله تعالى عنا خير الجزاء. كتبه الشيخ الدكتور خالد الزاهدي
Those who are firmly rooted in the world of books know that the commentary of al-Khabisi, from its birth and the rising of the light of its dawn, became the subject of scholars' scrutiny and the goal of noble students of knowledge; they study it and study it together, and revolve around the orbit of its unique gems and hunt the elusive ones of its benefits. And it is no wonder, for it is among the methodological curricula upon which scholars graduate in al-Azhar al-Sharif and other scientific assemblies and centers of Sharia studies in the east and west of the earth. It is sought after by students of Sharia knowledge and the scientific community, and it is among the most important books of logic that are considered a valuable source of this science. Among the latest eminent scholars who studied the book is our teacher, the accomplished scholar, the investigator, the usuli, Dr. Muhammad Salim Abu Asi. The origin of the commentary is a solid matn by al-Allama Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani in the two sciences of logic and kalam, called al-Tahzeeb. The first was blessed with acceptance, so its commentators were many; the second was afflicted with obscurity, so its mentioners were few—and Allah, exalted, has affairs in His creation. The most famous commentaries on Tahzeeb al-Mantiq are three: the commentary of al-Allama al-Jalal al-Diwani, and of the investigator Abdullah al-Yazawi, and the commentary of the scholar we are serving, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Khabisi, called al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb. Each of these commentaries had many glosses and notes, and among them the share of al-Tahzeeb was six, and the most important of them, the centerpiece of the necklace, and the jewel of the crown, was the gloss of al-Allama al-Dasuqi—may Allah have mercy on him—followed by the gloss of al-Allama al-Attar. But what grieves the soul is that this gloss—despite its preciousness—has not been printed in a good modern edition, and most of its modern publications are reproductions of its old editions. This gloss was printed in an old lithographic edition more than one hundred and thirteen years ago in the Kurdistan Scientific Press in Cairo, known for its proficiency and accuracy of printing, in the year 1328 AH. However, it lacked much of the diacritical marks, and it was found that many words and phrases were missing, errors and distortions occurred after collation with the manuscript, and it lacked punctuation and arrangement of its topics—this is something that students of knowledge suffer from while reading it with their teachers. If it had been free, correct, and sound, we would not have undertaken this great work that aims to serve students of knowledge. So we rolled up our sleeves of effort—by the grace of Allah, then by the encouragement of the dear brother, the famous Iraqi bookseller, Mr. Amir al-Uthmani, owner of Amir Library for Publishing and Distribution and Amir Center for Manuscript Verification in Kirkuk, who supported me in completing this precious work, provided me with manuscripts, and took care of it by reading, verifying, arranging, diacritizing, and correcting its texts, and producing it in the form you see—out of his eagerness to serve knowledge and its people. In conclusion, I thank Sheikh Abdul Karim Kani Sayfi, a teacher in Biyara al-Sharifa al-Sulaymaniyya, for the help he provided in reviewing the gloss and correcting some terms that require specialists, for he was worthy of it. May Allah reward him greatly. And I thank every noble brother who finds a mistake, an error, or a deficiency and contacts us to rectify it in its second edition, if Allah wills. Man is prone to forgetfulness and inadvertence, and a person is little by himself, much by his brothers, and some of us complete the others. May Allah reward you all with the best reward. Written by Sheikh Dr. Khalid al-Zahidi.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his edition of al-Dasuqi's gloss on al-Khabisi's commentary on al-Taftazani's Tahzeeb. He begins by asserting the well-known status of al-Khabisi's commentary, noting its widespread acceptance and study among scholars and students, particularly in al-Azhar and other institutions. It is a core text in Islamic logic. The author then mentions that the original text (matn) is al-Tahzeeb by al-Taftazani, which was highly accepted and thus had many commentaries, whereas al-Taftazani's other work (likely al-Mutawwal or something) did not receive the same attention. He lists the three most famous commentaries: those by al-Diwani, al-Yazawi, and al-Khabisi. Each of these spawned its own glosses (hawashi), and the most important gloss on al-Khabisi's commentary is that of al-Dasuqi, followed by that of al-Attar. However, the author laments that al-Dasuqi's gloss, despite its value, has not been properly edited and printed; existing editions are photographic reproductions of an old lithographic print from 1328 AH, which contains many errors, omissions, and lacks diacritics and proper organization. This causes difficulty for students. Therefore, the author undertook this new edition, with the support of Amir al-Uthmani, who provided manuscripts and assistance. He also acknowledges Sheikh Abdul Karim Kani Sayfi for reviewing the gloss and correcting terminology. The author invites readers to report any errors for correction in a future edition, emphasizing human fallibility and the collaborative nature of scholarship.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Necessity of Textual Precision in Islamic Scholarship
Editor describes the need for a corrected edition and thanks contributors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify common textual errors in Islamic manuscripts and explain why collation with a manuscript is essential for accurate teaching.

Core Idea
Textual precision preserves the integrity of Islamic knowledge from transmission errors.

In the editor's preface, we learn that even published editions can contain errors that hinder students. This lesson explores the Islamic science of tahqeeq (critical editing) and why every serious student must understand the need to verify texts against manuscripts.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the problem
The editor explicitly states that the previous edition lacked precision (ضبط), contained omissions, errors, and distortions after collation with the manuscript. This is a common issue in printed texts.
Note the Arabic terms: الضبط (dabt) for precision, المخطوط (makhtut) for manuscript.
2
Identify types of textual errors
The editor mentions missing words and phrases (سقط), errors and distortions (أخطاء وتحريف), and lack of punctuation and arrangement (علامات الترقيم والترتيب). Classify errors into omission, corruption, and formatting.
3
Understand the purpose of collation
Collation (مقابلة بالمخطوط) is the process of comparing the printed edition to the manuscript to detect discrepancies. This ensures the text matches the original author's intent.
This is a fundamental step in tahqeeq (critical edition).
4
Appreciate the collaborative effort
The editor thanks multiple contributors: a publisher who provided manuscripts, a specialist who corrected terms, and readers who report errors. This shows that textual accuracy is a communal responsibility.

Commentary
This passage is the editor's preface, explaining the need for a new corrected edition of the book. The editor begins by noting that the previous edition, though printed in Kurdistan al-Ilmiyya Cairo in 1328 AH, lacked precision and contained many omissions, errors, and distortions identified after collation with the manuscript. It also lacked punctuation and proper organization of topics. Such deficiencies, he says, hinder students when reading the book with their teachers. Had the edition been correct and sound, this editorial work would not have been undertaken. The editor then describes his motivation and support from Mr. Amir al-‘Uthmani, who provided manuscripts and assisted in reading, verifying, arranging, recording, and correcting the texts, aiming to present it well for the service of knowledge. Finally, he thanks Sheikh Abdul Karim Kani Sayfi for reviewing footnotes and correcting specialist terms, and invites readers to report any errors for correction in a future edition, acknowledging human fallibility and the cooperative nature of knowledge.

Al-Dasooqi's Methodology: Blending Commentary with Original Analysis
Describes al-Dasooqi's approach, blending commentary with original analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of al-Dasooqi's methodological approach in his gloss and explain how it strengthens the integration of logic into Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Al-Dasooqi's methodology merges commentary with independent analysis, making logic indispensable for sound religious study.

Al-Dasooqi's gloss on Tadhheeb al-Mantiq is not just another commentary; it is an original work that discovers objective criteria for evaluating arguments. In this lesson, we will explore his blended commentary style and his emphasis on the role of logic in religious sciences, as described in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the unique aspects of al-Dasooqi's approach
Notice how the passage contrasts his methodology with other logicians. What does he discover? Look for phrases like 'discovering objective criteria' and 'differs from the rest'.
2
Understand the blended commentary style
How does he combine his words with the original text? The passage says he 'mixed his statements and commentary' making the two books into one. What is the effect of this style?
3
Connect logic to religious sciences
How does al-Dasooqi argue that logic strengthens religious study? Find the specific statement: 'the religious study becomes strong if logic is strong'. Also note the mention of usul al-fiqh and other sciences.

منهج العلامة الدسوقي في حاشيته: «التجريد الشافي على تذهيب المنطق الكافي» بدا منهج الدسوقي في حاشيته ماتعاً جداً من حيث الخصوصية والتميز؛ إذ يختلف عن شروح بقيَّة علماء المنطق، ويمتاز عنهم، حيث جد في اكتشاف المعايير الموضوعيَّة لتقييم الحجج التي يستخدمها البشر في تدعيم أفكارهم ومعتقداتهم، وكيفية تطبيق هذه المعايير، واتَّبع أسلوب الشرح الممزوج، فمزج بين عباراته وشرحه بأسلوب مكَّنه من جعل الكتابين كتاباً واحداً، يصعب الفصل بينهما. ركَّز الدسوقي على باب التصورات والتصديقات؛ فإن كانت التصورات سليمة جاء الحكم سليماً، ومَن لا يعرف المنطق ففي علمه خلل، لذلك فإنَّ الدراسة الشرعيَّة تُصبح قويَّةً إذا كان المنطق قويَّاً لا سيما وأنَّ كتاب التذهيب في شرح التهذيب شرح العلامة عبيد الله بن فضل الله الخبيصي - على تهذيب المنطق والكلام لسعد الدين مسعود التفتازاني - لطالما ظل في دائرة اهتمام الباحثين والطلاب المهتمين بالدراسات الفقهيَّة؛ حيث يندرج تهذيب المنطق والكلام ضمن نطاق تخصص علوم أصول الفقه والتخصصات قريبة الصلة من عقيدة وحديث وسيرة نبوية وغيرها من فروع العلوم الشرعية. فكان ذلك موضع اهتمام الدسوقي؛ حانًا من بعده أن يشمرّوا ويشدُّوا عزائمهم ويسيروا بنية صالحة في هذا المضمار، وأن يستفيدوا من مؤلفات وكتب هؤلاء الأكابر الذين سبقوهم في علم المنطق؛ شريطة الفهم وضبط المسائل. والمتتبع لمنهج الدسوقي يخلص إلى نتيجة مفادها أنَّه كان سيّاراً في ركب من علماء المنطق والكلام، لكنَّه رغم اتكائه على آراء من سبقوه؛ فقد كان ذا مذهب مستقل حسب طبيعة الموضوع المعالج والغرض المنشود من ورائه؛ يحلُّ مشاكله ويكشف غوامضه من دون تقليد لأحدٍ مهما علَتْ قدمه وارتفعت مكانته.
The methodology of the scholar al-Dasooqi in his gloss: 'al-Tajreed al-Shafi 'ala Tadhheeb al-Mantiq al-Kafi'. The methodology of al-Dasooqi in his gloss began very enjoyable in terms of specificity and distinction; it differs from the commentaries of the rest of the logicians and stands out from them, for he was diligent in discovering objective criteria for evaluating arguments used by humans to support their ideas and beliefs, and how to apply these criteria. He followed the blended commentary style, mixing his statements and commentary in a manner that enabled him to make the two books into one book, difficult to separate. al-Dasooqi focused on the topic of concepts (tasawwurat) and assents (tasdiqat); if concepts are sound, the judgment comes sound, and whoever does not know logic has a defect in his knowledge. Therefore, the religious study becomes strong if logic is strong, especially since the book 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahdheeb' by al-Khabisi on Tahdheeb al-Mantiq wal Kalam by Saad al-Din al-Taftazani has always been in the circle of interest of researchers and students interested in fiqh studies; because Tahdheeb al-Mantiq wal Kalam falls under the field of uṣūl al-fiqh and closely related disciplines like creed, hadith, prophetic biography, and other branches of religious sciences. So that was the focus of al-Dasooqi's interest; he urged those after him to roll up their sleeves and strengthen their determinations and proceed with good intention in this field, and to benefit from the works and books of these greats who preceded them in logic, provided they understand and master the issues. And one who follows al-Dasooqi's methodology concludes that he was a traveler in the caravan of logicians and theologians, but despite his reliance on the views of those before him, he had an independent school of thought according to the nature of the subject under treatment and the desired purpose behind it; he solved its problems and uncovered its obscurities without imitating anyone, however great his standing and elevated his status.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a front_matter description of the methodology of the scholar al-Dasooqi in his gloss on the logical work 'Tadhheeb al-Mantiq'. It opens by naming his gloss 'al-Tajreed al-Shafi' and immediately highlights its distinctive character: al-Dasooqi's approach is uniquely enjoyable and specific, differing from other commentaries. His main innovation is the discovery of objective criteria for evaluating human arguments and their application. He employed a 'blended commentary' style, merging his own words with the original text so seamlessly that the two become one book. The passage then emphasizes al-Dasooqi's focus on the two fundamental branches of logic: tasawwurat (concepts) and tasdiqat (assents), arguing that correctness in concepts leads to correct judgments, and that ignorance of logic implies a defect in knowledge. This makes religious study ('al-dirasa al-shar'iyya) strong only when logic is strong. The author connects this to the importance of 'Tahdheeb al-Mantiq wal Kalam' by al-Taftazani and its commentary by al-Khabisi, noting its relevance to usul al-fiqh and other Islamic sciences. al-Dasooqi then exhorts students to diligently study logic, benefiting from the works of earlier masters while ensuring proper understanding. Finally, the passage characterizes al-Dasooqi as an independent thinker: though he relied on earlier authorities, he did not imitate them blindly but had his own method suited to each subject. This passage thus serves as an introduction to the work, setting the stage for the logical content to follow.

Al-Attar's Hashiyah: Method and Motivation
Author describes the need for al-Attar's hashiah and his corrective methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the problems al-Attar identified in earlier glosses on al-Tadhheeb and explain his corrective methodology.

Core Idea
Al-Attar's hashiah was a corrective response to textual distortions.

This lesson examines the preface to al-Attar's hashiah on al-Tadhheeb. We will explore why al-Attar felt compelled to write this gloss, what deficiencies he found in earlier works, and how he approached correcting them while maintaining respect for his predecessors. This sets the stage for understanding the role of super-commentaries in the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Map the textual layers
The passage mentions three layers: al-Tahdheeb (base text), al-Tadhheeb (commentary by al-Khabisi), and the hashiahs of Shaykh Yasin, Ibn Sa'id al-Maghribi, and al-Attar. Identify each and their relationships.
Al-Tadhheeb is a commentary on al-Tahdheeb; the hashiahs are super-commentaries.
2
Identify the defects al-Attar found
Al-Attar criticized two earlier hashiahs. For Shaykh Yasin's: distortion and misspelling from transmitters. For Ibn Sa'id's: excessive and unfair criticism, causing confusion.
These defects made the text difficult for students.
3
Extract al-Attar's corrective principles
Al-Attar's method included completing missing discussions, clarifying obscure points, and attributing quotes correctly, all while avoiding blind following or excessive criticism.
He also acknowledged the merits of earlier commentators.
4
Assess the outcome
The passage claims that al-Attar's hashiah achieved wide acceptance and was considered well-edited. Note that this is the author's evaluation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تأتي أهمية هذا الشَّرح في أنَّه يُظهر تطور منهج الدسوقي وشموله على كلّ شروح مسائل علم المنطق، فغدا هذا الشرح محط أنظار أهل المنطق المتأخرين والمعاصرين؛ الذين تناولوه بالشرح والتعليق.
منهج العلامة العطّار في حاشيته على التَّذهيب في شرح التهذيب للخبيصي سار العطّار على نهج المُجدِّدين الصَّادقين من السلف الصالح رضوان الله عليهم؛ الذين كانوا يصدعون بالحق ولا يخافون لومة لائم، فبعد دراسة مُمحَصة لشروح «التذهيب» للعلامة الخَبيصي؛ لاحظ العطّارُ أنَّه برغم وجازة ألفاظه وسلاسة معانيه فإنَّه كما قال: «محتاج إلى تتميم بعض مباحث وكشف غوامض»، وذلك لأنَّ حاشية العلامة الشَّيخ ياسين: «امتدَّ إليها من أيدي النَّقلة التحريف، وشوَّهوا محاسنها من كثرة التّصحيف»، وحين تلاه العلامة ابن سعيد المغربي: «شُغف بالاعتراض عليه، وولعَ بتعقبه في كل ما عوّل عليه، وقد ألجأه ذلك إلى الاعتساف وتجاوز الإنصاف ووقع في أوهام وأغاليط تُعكّر الأفهام». «فتوغَرَت بما ارتكباه للطَّالب المسالك، وتعشرت عليه المدارك، وصار الكتاب بسبب ذلك لغيرهما محتاجاً، ومُفتقراً لمن يسلك سبيل العدالة منهاجاً». قال رحمه الله: «فوضعتُ هذه الحاشية إسعافاً للطَّالبين، وإشفاقاً على المشتغلين». فعمد العطّار إلى توضيح ما تركاه مستوراً، وتتميم ما نقص من النقل، وإحالة ما نقلوه إلى أصحابه؛ دون أن يُنكر لهما الفضل بالشبق، ودون التَّردُّد في إعلان الحقِّ، بعيداً عن الجمود والتقليد. وقد وُفِّقَ في شرحه توفيقاً أقرّ له به القاصي والداني، العالم والطالب، فجاءت حاشيته نفيسة مُحرَّرة كما هي عادته في حواشيه رحمه الله تعالى.
The importance of this commentary comes from its showing the development of al-Dasuqi's methodology and its comprehensiveness over all commentaries on the topics of the science of logic. So this commentary became the focus of the eyes of later and contemporary logicians who dealt with it by explaining and annotating.
The methodology of al-'Allamah al-'Attar in his gloss on 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahdheeb' by al-Khabisi: al-'Attar followed the path of the truthful renewers among the righteous predecessors, may Allah be pleased with them, who proclaimed the truth and feared not the blame of a blamer. After a thorough study of the commentaries on 'al-Tadhheeb' by al-'Allamah al-Khabisi, al-'Attar noticed that despite the succinctness of its expressions and the smoothness of its meanings, it is, as he said: 'in need of completing some investigations and unveiling obscurities.' That is because the gloss of al-'Allamah al-Shaykh Yasin: 'distortion extended to it from the hands of the transmitters, and they disfigured its beauties from the frequency of misspelling.' And when al-'Allamah Ibn Sa'id al-Maghribi followed him: 'he became infatuated with objecting to it, and fond of criticizing it in everything he relied upon, and that forced him to be unfair and exceed justice, and he fell into illusions and errors that disturb understanding.' 'Thus the paths became difficult for the student due to what they committed, and the understandings became inaccessible, and the book due to that became in need of someone else, and dependent on one who follows the path of justice as a method.' He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'So I wrote this gloss to help students and out of compassion for those engaged in study.' So al-'Attar proceeded to clarify what they left hidden, complete what was deficient in transmission, and refer what they transmitted back to its original sources, without denying them credit for the effort, and without hesitation in declaring the truth, far from stagnation and blind following. And he was successful in his explanation with a success acknowledged by near and far, scholar and student. So his gloss came out precious and well-edited, as is his custom in his glosses, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a preface describing the value of al-Dasuqi's commentary on al-Tahdheeb and the methodology of al-Attar in his own gloss (hashiyah) on al-Khabisi's al-Tadhheeb. The author begins by asserting the importance of al-Dasuqi's commentary for showing the evolution of his method and its comprehensive coverage of logical topics, making it a focal point for later scholars. Then he discusses al-Attar's approach: he followed the renewers among the Salaf who fearlessly proclaimed truth. After examining the earlier commentaries, al-Attar found that al-Khabisi's work, though succinct, needed completion of certain discussions and clarification of obscure points. Two earlier glosses—by Shaykh Yasin and Ibn Sa'id al-Maghribi—had introduced distortions and excessive criticism, making the text difficult for students. Al-Attar therefore wrote his gloss to rectify these issues: he clarified hidden matters, completed missing transmissions, and attributed statements to their correct sources. He did this without denying the merit of the earlier commentators and without compromising the truth. The passage ends by praising al-Attar's successful outcome. This is thus a methodological introduction to the hashiah, explaining its purpose and the problems it addresses.

التذهيب
التهذيب

Al-ʿAṭṭār's Motivation for Writing His Gloss on al-Tahdhīb
Editor describes why al-ʿAṭṭār wrote his ḥāshiya and his methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three specific problems al-ʿAṭṭār found in previous commentaries and explain how his methodology addressed them.

Core Idea
Al-ʿAṭṭār wrote his gloss to correct textual corruption and biased criticism, restoring accuracy and fairness.

This passage from the editor's introduction explains why the great scholar al-ʿAṭṭār felt compelled to write his own gloss on al-Khabīṣī's commentary on al-Tahdhīb. Understanding his motivation reveals the high standards of scholarly integrity in the Islamic tradition. By the end, you will be able to articulate the precise flaws he identified and the principles he followed to rectify them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two earlier commentaries al-ʿAṭṭār evaluated
Find the names: Shaykh Yāsīn and Ibn Saʿīd al-Maghribī. Note what each contributed to the commentary tradition on al-Khabīṣī's work.
These are the predecessors whose works al-ʿAṭṭār studied before writing his own.
2
Analyze the problems al-ʿAṭṭār found in each
For Yāsīn's gloss: textual corruption (taṣḥīf) by copyists. For Ibn Saʿīd's: excessive criticism and unfairness. The result was confusion for students.
Note the specific Arabic terms: التحريف and التصحيف.
3
Extract al-ʿAṭṭār's three corrective actions
He clarifies unclear points, completes missing transmissions, and attributes statements to original sources. He also acknowledges previous scholars' merits while declaring truth.
These actions correspond to توضيح, تتميم, and إحالة.
4
Understand his guiding principles
He followed the method of truthful renewers, without fear of blame, avoiding rigidity and blind imitation.
This reflects the adab of scholarly criticism in Islam.

منهج العلامة العطّار في حاشيته على التَّذهيب في شرح التهذيب للخبيصي سار العطّار على نهج المُجدِّدين الصَّادقين من السلف الصالح رضوان الله عليهم ؛ الذين كانوا يصدعون بالحق ولا يخافون لومة لائم، فبعد دراسة مُمحَصة لشروح «التذهيب» للعلامة الخَبيصي ؛ لاحظ العطّارُ أنَّه برغم وجازة ألفاظه وسلاسة معانيه فإنَّه كما قال : مُحتاج إلى تتميم بعض مباحث وكشف غوامض»، وذلك لأنَّ حاشية العلامة الشَّيخ ياسين: «امتدَّ إليها من أيدي النَّقلة التحريف، وشوَّهوا محاسنها من كثرة التّصحيف»، وحين تلاه العلامة ابن سعيد المغربي: «شُغف بالاعتراض عليه، وولعَ بتعقبه في كل ما عوّل عليه، وقد ألجأه ذلك إلى الاعتساف وتجاوز الإنصاف ووقع في أوهام وأغاليط تُعكّر الأفهام . «فتوغَرَت بما ارتكباه للطَّالب المسالك، وتعشرت عليه المدارك، وصار الكتاب بسبب ذلك لغيرهما محتاجاً، ومُفتقراً لمن يسلك سبيل العدالة منهاجاً». قال رحمه الله: فوضعتُ هذه الحاشية إسعافاً للطَّالبين، وإشفاقاً على المشتغلين . فعمد العطّار إلى توضيح ما تركاه مستوراً، وتتميم ما نقص من النقل، وإحالة ما نقلوه إلى أصحابه ؛ دون أن يُنكر لهما الفضل بالشبق، ودون التَّردُّد في إعلان الحقِّ، بعيداً عن الجمود والتقليد . وقد وُفِّقَ في شرحه توفيقاً أقرّ له به القاصي والداني، العالم والطالب، فجاءت حاشيته نفيسة مُحرَّرة كما هي عادته في حواشيه رحمه الله تعالى .
The methodology of al-ʿAllāmah al-ʿAṭṭār in his gloss on al-Tahdhīb fī Sharḥ al-Tahdhīb by al-Khabīṣī: al-ʿAṭṭār followed the path of the truthful renewers from the righteous predecessors, may Allah be pleased with them, who proclaimed the truth and feared not the blame of any blamer. After a thorough study of the commentaries on 'al-Tahdhīb' by al-ʿAllāmah al-Khabīṣī, al-ʿAṭṭār observed that despite its concise wording and smooth meanings, it was, as he said, 'in need of completing some topics and unveiling obscurities.' This was because the gloss of al-ʿAllāmah al-Shaykh Yāsīn had been subject to distortion by the transmitters, who disfigured its beauties through frequent textual corruption. And when al-ʿAllāmah Ibn Saʿīd al-Maghribī succeeded him, he became engrossed in objecting to him and addicted to criticizing him in everything he relied upon, which led him to unfairness and exceeding the bounds of justice, and he fell into errors and fallacies that cloud understanding. Thus the paths became difficult for the student due to what they both committed, and the avenues became thorny, and the book thereby became in need of someone else, dependent on one who would tread the path of fairness as a method. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'So I wrote this gloss to assist students and out of compassion for those engaged in study.' So al-ʿAṭṭār proceeded to clarify what they left obscure, complete what was missing from transmission, and attribute what they transmitted to its rightful owners, without denying them merit in precedence, and without hesitation in declaring the truth, far from rigidity and blind imitation. He was granted success in his explanation, a success acknowledged by near and far, scholar and student, and thus his gloss came out as a precious, well-edited work, as is his custom in his glosses, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a prefatory note explaining the background and methodology of al-ʿAṭṭār's gloss (ḥāshiya) on al-Khabīṣī's commentary on al-Tahdhīb. It begins by stating that al-ʿAṭṭār followed the approach of the truthful renewers among the righteous predecessors, who were bold in proclaiming truth without fear of blame. After a careful study of al-Khabīṣī's work, al-ʿAṭṭār noted that, although the text was concise and smooth, it needed supplementation in certain discussions and clarification of obscure points. This need arose because the earlier gloss by Shaykh Yāsīn had suffered from textual corruption and distortion by later copyists, and the subsequent commentary by Ibn Saʿīd al-Maghribī was overly critical, focusing on objections and faults, leading to errors and confusion. As a result, the path for students became difficult. Therefore, al-ʿAṭṭār wrote his gloss to assist students and out of compassion for those studying. His method was to clarify what was left obscure, complete missing transmissions, and attribute statements to their original sources, while acknowledging the merits of previous scholars and being unhesitant in declaring the truth, avoiding rigidity and blind imitation. The passage concludes that his gloss was well-received and considered a precious, well-edited work. All examples here are from the text itself, which discusses scholarly works and their transmission, fitting within the Islamic scholarly tradition.

التذهيب
التصحيف

Al-Sharnubi's Commentary Methodology
Describes al-Sharnubi's method and qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of al-Sharnubi's commentary methodology as described in the introduction.

Core Idea
Al-Sharnubi's commentary combines tradition and independence to produce a clear, error-free guide.

This passage is not about logical rules, but about how the commentator al-Sharnubi approached his work. Understanding his methodology helps you trust the commentary's reliability and appreciate its place in the logical tradition. The passage describes his deep study of earlier works, his independence of thought, and his aim to clarify difficult points.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text type
Recognize that this is a front-matter introduction, not a logical argument. The passage describes the author's method and qualities, not content.
Do not look for logical form here.
2
Extract al-Sharnubi's qualities
List the attributes mentioned: brilliant, thorough, in harmony with earlier scholars, independent, fair, clear, dedicated.
These qualities establish the authority of the commentary.
3
Understand the textual layers
Identify the three layers: matn (al-Tadhhib), sharh (al-Khabisi), hashiya (al-Dusuqi and al-Attar), and ta'liq (al-Sharnubi). Note how al-Sharnubi engages with all.
This hierarchy is common in Islamic scholarly works.
4
Analyze his method
Al-Sharnubi follows the path of great logicians, but also expresses his own opinion freely. He extracts benefits from the hashias, corrects gaps, and aims to remove complexity.
His method balances tradition and originality.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهج العلامة الشَّرنوبي
مُمخّصاً
منهج العلامة الشرنوبي
في التعليق على «التَّذهيب» وحاشيتي الدسوقي والعطار سار الشرنوبي في تعليقه على الشَّرح والحاشيتين على خُطا قدامى فحول علماء المنطق، فبدا عبقريَّاً فذَاً، مُمسكاً بعلم المنطق من أطرافه، واصلاً ليله بنهاره، في حواشي الكتاب مفتشاً في أمهات كتب المنطق القديمة؛ حتّى ظهر بهذه الحُلَّة البديعة الخالية من التصحيف والتَّحريف وبدا الشَّرنوبي متماهياً مع كلِّ من الخبيصي والدسوقي والعطّار وكأنَّه كان معاصراً لهم؛ مبدياً رأيه بتعليقات تجمع بين العدل والصراحة، مُتَّخِذاً من حريَّة الرَّأي واستقلال الفكر سلاحاً، بأسلوب خال عن المواربة والغموض، باذلاً جهد ما استطاع ليُزيل التعقيدات في الأسلوب ورد في شرح كلِّ من المُحقِّق الدُّسوقي والخبر العطّار ؛ حتَّى كاد أن يبزّ أقرانه
الَّذِي
في غير موضع.
وقد وُفِّقَ في استخراج ما في سطور الحاشيتين من فوائد، وفكك ما فيها من رموز وطلاسم تستعصي على القارئ ؛ آخذاً على نفسه تصحيح ما فيها من ثغرات؛ معلّقاً على الشرح والحاشيتين معاً ؛ مُضحياً بثمين ،وقته، فظهرت درر كانت كامنة من غزارة علمه وسعة اطلاعه، وجاء التَّعليق وافياً بالغرض مبيناً للموضوعات الصعبة الشائكة؛ في شرح يتناسب مع روح العصر .
The methodology of the scholar al-Sharnubi. Summarized. The methodology of al-Sharnubi in commenting on al-Tadhhib and the two hashias of al-Dusuqi and al-Attar. Al-Sharnubi proceeded in his commentary on the explanation and the two supercommentaries upon the path of the great leading scholars of logic. Thus he appeared brilliantly, unique, grasping logic from all its sides, connecting his night to his day, in the margins of the book, searching in the authoritative books of ancient logic, until he appeared in this splendid garment free of errors and distortions. And al-Sharnubi appeared in harmony with each of al-Khabisi, al-Dusuqi, and al-Attar, as if he were contemporary with them, expressing his opinion with commentaries that combined justice and frankness, taking freedom of opinion and independence of thought as a weapon, in a style free of equivocation and obscurity, exerting as much effort as he could to remove complexities in the style found in the explanations of both the investigator al-Dusuqi and the scholar al-Attar, until he nearly surpassed his peers in many places. And he succeeded in extracting the benefits contained in the lines of the two hashias, and deciphering the symbols and riddles that baffle the reader, taking upon himself to correct the gaps in them, commenting on both the explanation and the two hashias together, sacrificing his precious time. Thus appeared pearls that were hidden, due to the abundance of his knowledge and breadth of his reading. And the commentary came fulfilling the purpose, clarifying difficult and thorny topics, in an explanation suited to the spirit of the age.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter description of the author al-Sharnubi's methodology and qualities in writing his commentary on the logic text 'al-Tadhhib' along with the supercommentaries (hashiyas) of al-Dusuqi and al-Attar. The author opens by stating that al-Sharnubi followed the path of the great logicians of the past, indicating that he was deeply rooted in the tradition. He describes al-Sharnubi as a genius who thoroughly mastered logic and tirelessly examined ancient sources, resulting in a commentary free of errors and distortions. The passage emphasizes that al-Sharnubi was in harmony with earlier commentators like al-Khabisi, al-Dusuqi, and al-Attar, as if he were their contemporary, yet he expressed his own opinions with fairness and clarity. He is credited with extracting valuable benefits from the two hashias, deciphering their obscure symbols, and correcting their gaps. The author praises al-Sharnubi's dedication and the resultant work that clarifies difficult topics in a style appropriate for the modern era. This passage serves to introduce the student to the nature of the commentary they are about to study, highlighting its reliability and depth.

Key Terms
التَّذهيب
حاشية
تعليق

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Understanding Front Matter in Islamic Logic Texts
Introduction to commendatory verses for a logic text edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of taqariz (commendatory verses) and hawaashi (glosses) in an Islamic logic text, and explain how front matter prepares the reader for the main text.

Core Idea
Front matter in Islamic scholarly editions is a map of scholarly lineage and authority.

Before diving into the logical content of a classic text like al-Tadhheeb, the reader is often greeted by front matter that establishes the work's scholarly credentials. This page introduces the commendatory verses (taqariz) that endorse the edition, along with the names of the commentators whose glosses accompany the text. Understanding this front matter is essential for appreciating the scholarly context and transmission of the logical knowledge you will study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Components
Look at the page and note the key elements: the title 'تقاريظ جليلة' (Great Praises), the name of the author of the exposition (Sheikh Muhammad Abdul Majeed al-Sharnubi), the main text (al-Tadhheeb by al-Khubaysi), and the two glosses (by al-Dasooqi and al-Attar).
This tells you who is involved in this edition.
2
Understand the Function of Taqariz
Taqariz are written endorsements by respected scholars. They serve to validate the work and guide readers on its importance and reliability. In logic texts, this helps establish the authority of the commentary and the edition.
Not all editions have taqariz; their presence indicates a formal scholarly production.
3
Recognize the Role of Glosses (Hawashi)
The edition includes two glosses (hashiyah) by well-known scholars. Glosses are marginal notes or super-commentaries that explain or critique the main text. They are essential for advanced study, as they show how later scholars engaged with the original.
The two glosses here are by al-Dasooqi and al-Attar, both respected in the Islamic logic tradition.
4
Relate Front Matter to the Study of Logic
This page is not just a formality; it tells you that the text you are about to study has been reviewed and endorsed by scholars. It also alerts you that the edition includes scholarly apparatus that you can use to deepen your understanding.
When you encounter a difficult passage in al-Tadhheeb, the glosses may provide the clarification you need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقاريظ جليلة لتقرير حضرة صاحب الأستاذ الشيخ الفضلية محمد عبد المجيد الشنوبي على كتاب التذهيب للخبيصي بحاشيتي الدسوقي والعطار نثبتها مرتبة حسب ورودها
Great Praises. For the exposition of His Excellency the Master Sheikh al-Fadliyya Muhammad Abdul Majeed al-Sharnubi on the book al-Tadhheeb by al-Khubaysi with the two glosses of al-Dasooqi and al-Attar. We record them arranged according to their order.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a front matter page introducing the taqariz (commendatory verses) that accompany this edition. It states that the taqariz are written by Sheikh Muhammad Abdul Majeed al-Sharnubi, referred to with honorific titles. The work in question is al-Tadhheeb by al-Khubaysi, a logic text, and this edition includes the two glosses (hawashi) of al-Dasooqi and al-Attar. The editor notes that the praises are arranged in the order they appear. This page serves as a bibliographic introduction, indicating the scholarly endorsements included in the book.

Key Terms
تقاريظ (taqariz): Commendatory verses or praises written by scholars to endorse a book or edition.
تقرير (taqrir): In this context, an elaboration or exposition of a text, often a commentary or explanation. [Note: In logic texts, taqrir can also mean 'establishment' or 'verification' of a proposition.]
حاشية (hashiyah): A marginal gloss or super-commentary on a main text; here, the two glosses by al-Dasooqi and al-Attar on al-Tadhheeb. [Note: Hashiyah is a standard genre in Islamic scholarship, ranging from short marginal notes to extensive independent commentaries.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'باحثيتي الدسوقي والعطار' refer to in this passage?
A) Two commentaries written by al-Dasooqi and al-Attar on a different book
B) Two glosses (hawashi) on al-Tadhheeb by al-Dasooqi and al-Attar
C) The names of the authors of al-Tadhheeb
D) The titles of the commendatory verses

Key Takeaway
This front matter page introduces the scholarly endorsements and apparatus that accompany the logic text al-Tadhheeb, establishing its credibility and guiding the reader on the resources available for study.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find an edition of al-Tadhheeb (or any classic Islamic logic text) and locate its front matter. List all the elements: title, author, commentators, any taqariz or introductory remarks. Summarize what each element tells you about the work's scholarly lineage.
?
Using the list of taqariz scholars from this edition, research one of them (e.g., al-Dasooqi or al-Attar) and write a short paragraph on their contribution to logic studies, citing examples of their other works.

The Role of Taqariz in Islamic Logic Education
Teachers of logic at Al-Azhar endorse the new edition with commentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose and components of a logic textbook commendation (taqriz) and its significance for Islamic education.

Core Idea
Taqariz are scholarly endorsements that ensure the reliability and trustworthiness of logic textbooks.

This passage is not a logical argument, but it reveals how the Islamic logical tradition is transmitted through scholarly collaboration. The teachers at Al-Azhar endorse a new edition of al-Tadhheeb, a standard logic text, praising the editor's efforts to include authoritative commentaries. Understanding this front matter helps us appreciate the care taken to preserve accurate logical knowledge for students of Shari'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
The passage is a commendation (taqriz) from logic teachers at Al-Azhar for a new edition of al-Tadhheeb.
This sets the context for the textbook's trustworthiness.
2
Identify the key elements
The edition includes the base text by al-Khabisi, with two footnotes by al-Dusuqi and al-Attar, edited by al-Sharnubi.
Each element contributes to the scholarly value of the book.
3
Understand the significance of footnotes (hashiyah)
Footnotes provide explanations and corrections, making the text more accessible for students.
They function as a layered commentary tradition.
4
Recognize the collaborative nature
The edition was produced by a publishing company, an editor, and endorsed by professors, showing the communal effort in Islamic education.
This reflects the collective responsibility for knowledge transmission.
5
Connect to the broader tradition
Such endorsements (taqariz) are common in Islamic scholarship, serving as quality control and guiding students to reliable sources.
They help preserve the integrity of the logical sciences.

بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ
الحمدُ للهِ الَّذِي ميز الإنسان بالعقل وهداه سبل التفكير، والصَّلاة والسَّلامُ على سيِّدِنَا مُحمَّدٍ صاحبِ البرهان المنيرِ، وَعَلى آله وصحبه الذين عنوا بصيانة العقول، وسوَّرُوا المعقول والمنقول. وبعد» فَلَقَدْ أُسندت إلينا دراسة المنطقِ لِطلبة كُلِّيَّةَ الشَّرِيعَةِ في كتابِ التَّذهيبِ للعلامة عبيد الله بن فضل اللهِ الخَبيصي، أسكنه الله فسيحَ جَنَّتِهِ، فَاستَعَنَّا الله وأخذنا نبحثُ عَن الحواشي الَّتي تكشفُ الحجابَ عَن هذا الكتاب، حتَّى قيَّضَ اللَّهُ لَنَا زميلنا العلامةَ الشَّيخَ مُحمَّد عبد المجيدِ الشَّرنوبي، فشمَّرَ عن ساعد الجد، وعمل معَ أصحاب شركة مكتبة ومطبعةِ مُصطفى البابي الحلبي وأولاده بمصر التي تعهَّدَتْ بِإخراج الكتابِ مقروناً بحاشيتيه الجليلتين : حاشية المحقِّقِ «الدسوقي»، وَحاشية الحبرِ «العطّار) ولقد أسهر الأستاذُ الشَّرنوبي جفنه في تصحيح الكتابِ مَعَ الحاشِيَتَيْنِ حتَّى خطر في مُحلَّةٍ بديعةٍ، باديَ الرُّواء، خالياً مِنَ التَّصحيفِ والتَّحريف، يختالُ بين كتب المنطق القديمة والحديثة بتلك الأذيالِ الدَّمقسيَّةِ الَّتي طَرَّزَهُ بها قلمُ الأستاذ، فَقَرَّبَ بها البعيد من الشَّوارد ، وذلَّلَ بها الأبيَّ من الأوابد ، جزى الله زميلنا خير الجزاء، وهدانا وإيَّاه سواء السبيل.
أحمد ((
مد كامل مُحَمَّد بدران، موسی اللَّبَاد، مُحَمَّد متولّي جيرة الله ، شبل يحيى.
Splendid endorsements. For the report of His Excellency the Professor, the Virtuous Sheikh Muhammad Abd al-Majid al-Sharnubi, on the book 'al-Tadhheeb' by al-Khabisi, with the two footnotes of al-Dusuqi and al-Attar. We present them arranged according to their occurrence.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who distinguished man with intellect and guided him to the ways of thinking. Peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad, possessor of the luminous proof, and upon his family and companions who cared for the preservation of intellects and fortified the rational and transmitted knowledge. To proceed: Indeed, the study of logic was entrusted to us for the students of the Faculty of Shari'a in the book 'al-Tadhheeb' by the scholar Ubayd Allah ibn Fadl Allah al-Khabisi, may Allah grant him spaciousness in His paradise. So we sought help from Allah and began searching for footnotes that unveil the veil from this book, until Allah facilitated for us our colleague, the scholar Sheikh Muhammad Abd al-Majid al-Sharnubi. He rolled up his sleeves of diligence and worked with the owners of Mustafa al-Babi al-Halabi and Sons Company in Egypt, which undertook to produce the book accompanied by its two noble footnotes: the footnote of the investigator al-Dusuqi and the footnote of the learned al-Attar. Indeed, Sheikh al-Sharnubi kept his eyes awake in correcting the book along with the two footnotes until it appeared in a wonderful form, with beautiful appearance, free from distortion and alteration, strutting among old and modern logic books with those Damascene tails that the professor's pen embroidered upon it. He thereby brought near the distant elusive ones and tamed the rebellious ones. May Allah reward our colleague with the best reward and guide us and him to the straight path. Ahmad ((
Mud Kamal Muhammad Badran, Musa al-Labadd, Muhammad Mutawalli Jirah Allah, Shibl Yahya.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is front matter: a teacher's endorsement (kalam) for a new edition of al-Khabisi's 'al-Tadhheeb', which is a standard logic textbook. The teachers of logic at Al-Azhar's Faculty of Shari'a explain how they needed a clear edition with commentaries to teach students. They praise their colleague al-Sharnubi for editing the text with the footnotes of al-Dusuqi and al-Attar, ensuring accuracy and removing errors. The passage highlights the importance of logic in Islamic education, specifically for Shari'a studies, and the collaborative effort to produce a reliable textbook. The teachers express gratitude and pray for reward for the editor.

التذهيب
الخبيصي
حاشية
المنطق

Key Takeaway
The front matter of a logic textbook reflects the scholarly chain of transmission and the collaborative effort to produce reliable educational materials for Shari'a students.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Role of Glosses in Al-Khabbisi's Al-Tadhheeb
Professors explain the need for this edition with the two important glosses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of glosses (hawashi) in teaching logic at Al-Azhar and explain how al-Sharnubi's edition made the text accessible.

Core Idea
Glosses unlock dense logical texts, making them teachable in Islamic seminaries.

The professors at Al-Azhar University were tasked with teaching logic using al-Khabbisi's commentary, al-Tadhheeb. They realized that the text alone was difficult for students, so they sought glosses (hawashi) to clarify it. This lesson explores how the editors combined the matn with two critical glosses to produce an accessible edition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the need for glosses
Read the professors' statement that they searched for glosses 'that would unveil the veil from this book.' Why was the original text difficult?
The text is a dense commentary on Tahzeeb al-Mantiq.
2
Identify the glossators
Find the names of the two scholars whose glosses were included: al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar. Note their titles: 'al-muhaqqiq' (the investigator) and 'al-hibr' (the scholar).
3
Evaluate the editor's work
Consider al-Sharnubi's role: he corrected the text and glosses, producing a clean edition 'free from distortion and alteration.' Why was this important for teaching?
Accuracy is crucial for logical instruction.
4
Connect to the broader tradition
Reflect on how glosses function in Islamic scholarly tradition: they expand, critique, or clarify earlier works. How does this edition exemplify that tradition?
Glosses are a key genre in Islamic intellectual history.

From the professors, teachers of logic at the Faculty of Islamic Law at Al-Azhar University
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful
Praise be to Allah who distinguished man with intellect and guided him to the ways of thinking, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad, possessor of the clear proof, and upon his family and companions who cared for the preservation of intellects and fortified the rational and transmitted. After: Indeed, the study of logic for students of the Faculty of Law was entrusted to us in the book 'Al-Tadhheeb' by the scholar 'Ubaydullah ibn Fadlullah al-Khabbisi, may Allah grant him spacious paradise. So we sought Allah's help and began searching for glosses that would unveil the veil from this book, until Allah facilitated for us our colleague, the eminent scholar Shaykh Muhammad 'Abd al-Majid al-Sharnubi. He rolled up his sleeves in earnestness and worked with the owners of the Mustafa al-Babi al-Halabi and Sons Printing and Publishing Company in Egypt, which undertook to produce the book accompanied by its two esteemed glosses: the gloss of the investigator al-Dasuqi and the gloss of the scholar al-'Attar. The professor al-Sharnubi spent sleepless nights correcting the book with the two glosses until it appeared in a beautiful garb, bright in appearance, free from distortion and alteration, strutting among old and new logic books with those Damascene tails that his pen adorned, thereby bringing near the distant elusive ones and taming the stubborn refractory ones. May Allah reward our colleague with the best reward and guide us and him to the straight path.
Ahmad
((
Mud? Kamil Muhammad Badran, Musa al-Labbad, Muhammad Mutawalli Jiratullah, Shibl Yahya.
?
·
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an introductory statement from the professors teaching logic at Al-Azhar University. It opens with the basmala and hamdala, praising Allah for bestowing intellect and guiding humanity to reasoning. The professors then explain that they were tasked with teaching logic using the book 'Al-Tadhheeb' by al-Khabbisi. They sought commentaries (hawashi) to clarify difficult points, and found their colleague al-Sharnubi willing to edit the book along with the glosses of al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar. The professors describe al-Sharnubi's diligent work, resulting in a clean, accurate edition that makes the subject accessible. The passage ends with signatures of the professors (Ahmad and four others). This is purely front matter, setting the context for the edition.

الخَبيصي
الدسوقي
العطّار

Key Takeaway
The edition of al-Tadhheeb with glosses by al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar demonstrates how scholarly collaboration and editorial work make complex logical texts accessible for teaching.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Purpose of a Commentary in Islamic Logic
Students describe difficulties with existing commentaries and praise the new edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the pedagogical role of a commentary and identify the qualities of a student-centered scholarly edition.

Core Idea
The best commentaries clarify, not complicate.

This commendation by third-year students at Al-Azhar reveals the real-world struggle with dense glosses and the value of a balanced annotation. It shows that a commentary's purpose is to serve the learner, not to display the commentator's depth. As you read, notice how the students' experience mirrors the purpose of logical instruction: to make knowledge accessible and retainable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Read the students' description of the glosses by al-'Attar and al-Dasuqi. What specific issues do they mention? Look for terms like 'تعقيدات في الأسلوب' (complexities in style) and 'اعتراضات كثيرة' (many objections).
2
Analyze the effect on learning
The students say they had to memorize without understanding ('نستظهر هذه الكلمات التي هي بالرموز في نظرنا أشبه'). Why does this happen? Consider how excessive complexity and weak objections prevent comprehension.
3
Examine the solution offered
What does al-Sharnubi do differently? The students praise his 'موقف المنصف' (position of a fair judge) and 'حد الوسط' (middle course). List the qualities they highlight: fairness, humility, abundant knowledge, and focus on clarifying topics.
4
Connect to the purpose of a commentary
Based on the passage, what is the ultimate goal of a commentary on a logical text? The students mention the book nearly left its purpose ('خرج الكتاب عن الغرض الذي أُلْفَ من أجله'). Al-Sharnubi's edition restores that purpose by making the material understandable.
