Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Grammar of 'Ba'd' in Islamic Commentaries
Al-Dasūqī's analysis of the word 'ba'd' and its grammatical status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the grammatical reason for the indeclinability of 'ba'd' in the commentator's introduction and explain the concept of partial relation.

Core Idea
‘Ba'd’ is indeclinable due to deletion of its complement and intention of a specific partial relation.

In the opening of his super-commentary, al-Dasūqī pauses to analyze the word 'ba'd' (وبعد). His explanation reveals a nuanced grammatical rule that distinguishes formal commentary writing from everyday speech. Understanding this rule will help you parse similar constructions in classical Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Locate 'ba'd' in the text
It appears as 'وبعد' at the beginning of the commentary body. Note its usual function as a locative adverb meaning 'after'.
2
Identify the grammatical rule
Al-Dasūqī states that it is 'ẓarf mabnī 'alā al-ḍamm' (a locative adverb built on ḍamma). This is unusual because locative adverbs are normally declinable.
3
Understand the deletion and intention
The reason given is 'li-ḥadhf al-muḍāf ilayhi wa-niyyat thubūt al-nisba al-juz'iyya' (due to deletion of the genitive complement and intention of the partial relation). The complement is the specific basmala and hamdala that precede, and the partial relation means the posteriority is tied only to those.
4
Respond to the objection
The hypothetical objection: partial relation normally requires two things (muḍāf and muḍāf ilayh). Why is it only attached to the muḍāf ilayh? Answer: because partiality is only realized with that specific muḍāf ilayh.
This is a subtle point about Arabic grammar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الشَّارح
صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وعلى آله وأصحابه المحمودين على الاتِّباع والتصديقِ، المسْعُودِينَ في مَنَاهجِ الصِّدقِ على التَّحقيقِ .
وبعد :
الدسوقي
يُسبق لها مثال باهرٌ ، وغالب دليلها لِمَنْ طعن فيها، وخصمه ، وإسناد البهر للدليل مجاز عقلي ؛ لأنَّ الباهر حقيقة النَّبي الله، لكن بالدليل، فالدليل آلة للبهرِ . و (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَحْمُودِيْنَ) أي : الَّذين حمدَهُمُ اللَّهُ ؛ أي : الَّذِينَ مَدحَهُم الله (على الاتِّباع) لِلنَّبيِّ (والتصديقِ) له فيما يقولُه ، وعطفُ التَّصديق على الاتِّباع عطفُ لازم على ملزوم. (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَسْعُوْدِيْنَ) أي : الَّذين حصلَتْ لهم السعادة. (قَوْلُهُ : فِي مَنَاهِج) مُتعلّق بمحذوف ؛ أي: لسلوكهم في مناهج؛ أي: طرقٍ الصدقِ، وَقولُهُ: (على التحقيقِ)؛ مُتعلّق بالمسعودين، والتَّحقيق يحتمل أَنْ يُرادَ بِهِ ضدُّ الشَّلِّ وهو اليقين؛ أي: الذين حصلَتْ لَهُمُ السَّعادةُ بِلَا شَكٍّ، ويحتمل أنَّ المراد على تحقيقهم الأشياء؛ أي : ذكرِهَا على الوجه الحقِّ؛ لأنَّ الصِّدقَ مِن أوصافهم، أو أنَّ المراد أنَّهم إذا ذكروا أحكاماً ذكرُوا لها دليلاً، وفي تقرير المسعودين ... إلخ؛ أي : الذين حصلت لهمُ السَّعادة على التحقيق بسببِ سلوكِ مناهج الصِّدْقِ، وشبَّهَ الصدق بمكان ذي طرقٍ على طريق المكنية، وإثبات المناهج تخييل. (قَوْلُهُ: وَبَعْدُ) هي ظرف مبني على الضَمّ؛ لحذف المضاف إليه ونيَّة ثبوتِ النّسبةُ الجزئيّةُ كَنسبةِ البعديَّةِ هنا للبسملة والحمدلةِ وَمَا مَعَهُمَا، لَا يُقالُ : إِنَّ النّسبة الجزئية لا تعقلُ إلَّا بينَ شَيئين كالمضاف والمضاف إليه، فَلِمَ جُعِلَت معنّى للمضاف إليه دون المضاف أيضاً ؟ والجواب : إنّها لَمَّا لم تتحقق جزئيتها إلا بالمضاف إليه الجزئي ؛ جُعِلتُ معنّى لهُ وَحدَه .
Introduction of the commentator: May Allah bless him and his family and his companions who are praised for following and believing, the fortunate ones in the paths of truth with verification. And after: Al-Dasuqi: A brilliant example precedes it, and most of its proof is for those who attack it, and his opponent, and attributing brilliance to the proof is a mental metaphor; because the brilliant is truly the prophecy of the Prophet, but by the proof, so the proof is an instrument of brilliance. And (his statement: the praised ones) meaning those whom Allah praised; i.e., those whom Allah praised (for following) the Prophet (and believing) in what he says, and the conjunction of belief upon following is a conjunction of necessary upon necessary. (His statement: the fortunate ones) meaning those who attained happiness. (His statement: in paths) is attached to a deleted [phrase]; i.e., for their conduct in paths; i.e., ways of truth, and his statement: (with verification) is attached to the fortunate ones, and verification can be intended as the opposite of doubt, i.e., certainty; meaning those who attained happiness without doubt, and it can be intended as their verification of things; i.e., mentioning them in the true manner; because truth is among their attributes, or that the meaning is that when they mention rulings they mention a proof for them, and in the exposition of the fortunate ones ... etc.; i.e., those who attained happiness with verification due to their conduct of the paths of truth, and he likened truth to a place with paths in a metaphorical way, and the affirmation of paths is imaginative. (His statement: 'and after') is a locative adverb built on damma; due to the deletion of the genitive complement and the intention of the partial relation, like the relation of 'posteriority' here to the basmala and the hamdala and what is with them. It is not said: The partial relation is only conceivable between two things like the additive and the additive to, so why was it made meaning for the additive to without the additive? The answer: Since its partially is not realized except with the partial additive to, it was made meaning for it alone.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the commentary (sharh) on the matn by al-Ḫabīṣī, which itself opens with the commentator's introduction praising the Prophet and his companions. Al-Dasūqī, the super-commentator, explains each phrase. First, he clarifies that the expression 'a brilliant example' (مثال باهر) refers to the miracle (mu'jiza) of the Prophet, and attributing 'brilliance' to the proof is a mental metaphor because the real agent is Allah. Then he explains the praise phrases: 'al-mahmūdīn' (the praised ones) are those whom Allah praised for following and believing in the Prophet. He notes that 'following' (ittibā') is the necessary condition and 'believing' (taṣdīq) is the necessary result, so the conjunction is of the necessary upon the necessary (عطف لازم على ملزوم). Next he explains 'al-mas'ūdīn' (the fortunate ones) as those who attained happiness, and discusses the meaning of 'taḥqīq' (verification): either certainty (yaqīn) or the act of verifying things correctly. He also analyzes the metaphor in 'manāhij al-ṣidq' (paths of truth) as a metaphorical comparison of truth to a place with paths. Finally, he delves into the grammar of the word 'ba‘d' (وبعد), stating that it is a locative adverb (ẓarf) that is built on ḍamma because the genitive complement (muḍāf ilayhi) is deleted, and the intention is a partial relation (nisba juz'iyya) — that is, the relation of 'posteriority' is not general but specifically to the basmala and hamdala that precede. He answers an objection: even though a partial relation normally requires two things (like mudāf and mudāf ilayh), here it is only attached to the mudāf ilayh because the partiality is not realized except with that specific mudāf ilayh. This passage is typical of front matter in a logical commentary, combining praise, theological clarification, and grammatical analysis.

Key Terms
بعد
النسبة الجزئية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the word 'بعد' built on ḍamma in the commentator's introduction?
A) Because it is a genitive complement
B) Because the speaker made a mistake
C) Because the genitive complement is deleted and a partial relation is intended
D) Because it is a preposition

Key Takeaway
The indeclinability of 'ba'd' in this context is a grammatical marker of a deleted but intentionally preserved complement.

Find another example in an Islamic text (e.g., a fatwa collection or a tafsir) where 'ba'd' is used at the beginning of a section. Determine if it is declinable or indeclinable and why.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Understanding Praise and Metaphor in the Commentary's Opening
Al-Dasūqī's explanation of the praise phrases and mental metaphor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relationship between following and believing in the praise of the companions and identify the mental metaphor in attributing brilliance to the proof.

Core Idea
Praise of the Prophet's companions is structured as necessary conditions, and brilliance is metaphorically attributed to the proof.

Al-Dasūqī begins his super-commentary by glossing the praise of the Prophet and his companions. He clarifies not only the meaning of the attributes but also the logical connections between them. He also points out a subtle metaphor: the proof is called 'brilliant' (bahir) even though true brilliance belongs to the Prophet's miracle.

Guided Path
1
Find the phrase 'mīthāl bāhir'
This is a proof of the Prophet's prophecy. Al-Dasūqī says attributing brilliance to the proof is a mental metaphor because the real brilliant thing is the miracle itself.
2
Understand the attributes of the companions
They are 'al-mahmūdīn' (praised) for two things: 'al-ittibā‘' (following) and 'al-taṣdīq' (believing). The conjunction is of necessary upon necessary.
3
Analyze the metaphor of 'manāhij al-ṣidq'
Truth is likened to a place with paths. This is a metaphorical expression (tashbīh balīgh) where the path is the way of truth.
4
Interpret 'al-mas‘ūdīn' (the fortunate ones)
Those who attained happiness due to their conduct on these paths. The term 'taḥqīq' can mean certainty or verification.

مُقَدِّمَةُ الشَّارح
صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وعلى آله وأصحابه المحمودين على الاتِّباع والتصديقِ، المسْعُودِينَ في مَنَاهجِ الصِّدقِ على التَّحقيقِ .
وبعد :
الدسوقي
يُسبق لها مثال باهرٌ ، وغالب دليلها لِمَنْ طعن فيها، وخصمه ، وإسناد البهر للدليل مجاز عقلي ؛ لأنَّ الباهر حقيقة النَّبي الله، لكن بالدليل، فالدليل آلة للبهرِ . و (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَحْمُودِيْنَ) أي : الَّذين حمدَهُمُ اللَّهُ ؛ أي : الَّذِينَ مَدحَهُم الله (على الاتِّباع) لِلنَّبيِّ (والتصديقِ) له فيما يقولُه ، وعطفُ التَّصديق على الاتِّباع عطفُ لازم على ملزوم. (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَسْعُوْدِيْنَ) أي : الَّذين حصلَتْ لهم السعادة. (قَوْلُهُ : فِي مَنَاهِج) مُتعلّق بمحذوف ؛ أي: لسلوكهم في مناهج؛ أي: طرقٍ الصدقِ، وَقولُهُ: (على التحقيقِ)؛ مُتعلّق بالمسعودين، والتَّحقيق يحتمل أَنْ يُرادَ بِهِ ضدُّ الشَّلِّ وهو اليقين؛ أي: الذين حصلَتْ لَهُمُ السَّعادةُ بِلَا شَكٍّ، ويحتمل أنَّ المراد على تحقيقهم الأشياء؛ أي : ذكرِهَا على الوجه الحقِّ؛ لأنَّ الصِّدقَ مِن أوصافهم، أو أنَّ المراد أنَّهم إذا ذكروا أحكاماً ذكرُوا لها دليلاً، وفي تقرير المسعودين ... إلخ؛ أي : الذين حصلت لهمُ السَّعادة على التحقيق بسببِ سلوكِ مناهج الصِّدْقِ، وشبَّهَ الصدق بمكان ذي طرقٍ على طريق المكنية، وإثبات المناهج تخييل. (قَوْلُهُ: وَبَعْدُ) هي ظرف مبني على الضَمّ؛ لحذف المضاف إليه ونيَّة ثبوتِ النّسبةُ الجزئيّةُ كَنسبةِ البعديَّةِ هنا للبسملة والحمدلةِ وَمَا مَعَهُمَا، لَا يُقالُ : إِنَّ النّسبة الجزئية لا تعقلُ إلَّا بينَ شَيئين كالمضاف والمضاف إليه، فَلِمَ جُعِلَت معنّى للمضاف إليه دون المضاف أيضاً ؟ والجواب : إنّها لَمَّا لم تتحقق جزئيتها إلا بالمضاف إليه الجزئي ؛ جُعِلتُ معنّى لهُ وَحدَه .

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Understanding the Commentator's Preface: Purpose and Terminology
The commentator states his motivation for writing this sharh on al-Tahdhib, praising its author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of a sharh as exemplified by the commentator's preface and define the key terms sa'adah, husna, and ziyadah as used in Islamic supplications.

Core Idea
The commentator's preface shows how a sharh both praises the matn and clarifies its language.

The commentator begins his sharh of al-Tahdhib with a supplication for the author, explaining the meaning of each term. This opening is not merely decorative; it sets the tone for the entire commentary. The careful parsing of words like sa'adah and husna demonstrates the rigorous method that will follow. Moreover, the commentator's discussion of the book's name reveals his approach to textual economy and his respect for the author's humility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the supplication and its components
Find the prayer phrase in Arabic. List the three boons requested: al-sa'adah, al-husna, and al-ziyadah.
The commentator begins with a supplication for the original author.
2
Define each requested boon according to the commentator
Using the commentary, extract the specific meanings: al-sa'adah is death upon faith, al-husna is Paradise, and al-ziyadah is seeing Allah or multiplied reward.
These definitions are not the common meanings; they are specified by the commentator.
3
Analyze the structure of the preface
Note how the sentence 'lamma ra'aytu...' is the object of the verb and spans the entire book. This shows the grammatical precision of the sharh.
The commentator identifies the long sentence as the direct object of 'yaqulu'.
4
Examine the justification for the book's name
Understand why the commentator uses the shorter name 'al-Tahdhib' instead of the full title. He states it is because the book became famous by that name, just as 'al-Sa'd' is used for Sa'd al-Din.
This reflects the commentator's attention to customary usage and economy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الشَّارِح
لهُ السَّعادة، ورَزَقَهُ الحُسنى وزيادة - : لَمَّا رأيتُ المختصر المسمَّى (التَّهْذِيبِ)، المنسوب إلى أفضل المحققين وأكمل المتأخّرينَ،
الدسوقي
ويمكنُ أنْ يجابَ : بأنَّ لِطلبِهِ ،معنّى، وهو احتمال أن يكونَ مِنَ القضاء المعلَّقِ على طلبه، وقال بعضُ : المراد بالسَّعادة؛ تَعلُّق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث ؛ أي: أتحفَهُ وَوَهبَهُ السَّعادة؛ أي: الموتَ على الإيمان؛ أي: رزقَهُ إيَّاها وأبرزها لهُ خارجاً فيما لا يزالُ، أو قدَّر الله ؛ أي: يسَّرَ اللهُ وهيَّاً .
(قَوْلُهُ : السَّعَادَةَ) أي : الموت على الإيمان، والجملةُ مُعترضةٌ بين القولِ ومقوله ؛ لإنشاء الدُّعاءِ لِنَفْسِه .
(قَوْلُهُ: الحُسْنَى) أي: الجنَّة .
(قَوْلُهُ: وَزِيَادَةٌ) أي : رؤيةَ اللهِ في الجنَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ ألذ الأشياء، أو المراد بالحُسنَى : التَّوابُ المترتِّبُ على الأعمال، وبالزِّيادةِ : التَّوابُ الحاصل بالمضاعفة.
(قَوْلُهُ : لَمَّا ... إلخ) مقول القول، فهو إلى آخرِ الكتاب في محلّ نصب مقول القول، وليس قوله : لَمَّا رأيتُ ... إلخ، وحدَه له محل ؛ إذ جزء المقول لا محلّ لهُ على التحقيق.
(قَوْلُهُ : بِالتَّهْذِيبِ) هوَ في الأصل معناه : التَّخليصُ مِنَ الحشوِ والتَّطويل، وفي تسمية الكتابِ بذلكَ مُبالغةٌ في تخليصه منهما، فكأنَّه نفس التخليص على حد : زيد عدل، وفي قوله : المسمَّى (بالتهذيب) اقتصارُ على جزء العلم وتصرُّف في بالحذف؛ إذ اسمُهُ: «تهذيب الكلام في عِلْمَي المنطقِ والكلام، والمسوِّغُ لِلشَّارِحِ في التَّصرُّفِ شهرتُهُ بذلكَ كَمَا قالُوا : السَّعدُ في «سعدِ الدِّين».
(قَوْلُهُ : الْمَنْسُوْبَ) صفةٌ للمختصر، وقالَ ذلكَ؛ إشارةً إلى أنَّهُ لمْ يقطع بكونِهِ للسَّعْدِ، وذلك لأنَّهُ لم يذكر اسمه في أوَّلِهِ تواضُعاً .
(قَوْلُهُ : وَأَكْمَل ...إلخ) إلخ) عطف لازم على ملزوم.
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ: الحُسْنَى) هي الجنَّةُ ، و(الزّيادةُ): هي النَّظر إلى وجهه الكريم، أو المثوبة الحسنى، والزّيادة ما يزيد عليها ؛ تفضّلاً منهُ ومِنَّةٌ ، لِقولِهِ تعالى : وَيَزِيدُهُم مِّن فَضْلِهِ ﴾ [النِّسَاء : ١٧٣] .
Commentator's Preface: For him [the author] is felicity, and may He grant him the best and an increase. When I saw the abridgement called al-Tahdhib, attributed to the best of the investigators and the most complete of the later ones, al-Dasuqi: And it can be answered that requesting it has a meaning, and it is that it may be of the suspended decree (al-qada' al-mu'allaq) dependent on the request. And some said: By 'felicity' is meant the attachment of the temporal actual power; i.e., He gifted him and granted him felicity, i.e., death upon faith; i.e., He provided him with it and manifested it to him externally in the future. Or 'qaddara' means He facilitated and prepared. (His saying: 'al-sa'adah') i.e., death upon faith, and the sentence is parenthetical between the saying and its object, to compose a supplication for himself. (His saying: 'al-husna') i.e., Paradise. (His saying: 'wa ziyadah') i.e., seeing Allah in Paradise, which is the most delightful of things, or the intended meaning of 'al-husna' is the reward dependent on deeds, and 'al-ziyadah' is the reward obtained by multiplication. (His saying: 'lamma... etc.') is the object of the saying, so it is in the accusative case as the object of the saying until the end of the book, and not only his saying 'lamma ra'aytu...' has a grammatical function; since part of the object has no function according to verification. (His saying: 'bi-al-Tahdhib') originally means purification from superfluity and prolixity, and in naming the book it is an exaggeration in purifying it from them, as if it is the very purification, like 'Zayd is justice'. And in his saying 'al-musamma bi-al-Tahdhib' there is restriction to part of the science and a modification by deletion; for its name is 'Tahdhib al-Kalam fi 'Ilmay al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam', and what justifies the commentator's modification is its fame by that, as they said: 'al-Sa'd' for 'Sa'd al-Din'. (His saying: 'al-mansub') is an adjective for the abridgement, and he said that to indicate that he does not definitively assert it is by al-Sa'd, because he did not mention his name at its beginning out of humility. (His saying: 'wa akmal... etc.') is a conjunction of a necessary attribute with its essence. al-Attar: (His saying: 'al-husna') is Paradise, and 'al-ziyadah' is looking at His noble face, or the good reward, and the increase is what exceeds it as a favor and grace, due to His saying: 'and He increases them from His bounty' [al-Nisa 4:173].
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is the **opening of the commentator's preface** (muqaddimat al-sharih). The commentator begins with a supplication for the original author of al-Tahdhib: that he may attain felicity (al-sa'adah, i.e., death upon faith), the best reward (al-husna, i.e., Paradise), and an increase (ziyadah, e.g., seeing Allah). The commentator (likely Dasuqi) then explains that the prayer 'qaddarallah' in the earlier line is meaningful if it is part of a suspended decree. He then proceeds to parse the words of the author: 'al-sa'adah' is death upon faith; 'al-husna' is Paradise; 'ziyadah' is seeing Allah or multiplied reward. The statement 'lamma ra'aytu...' (When I saw...) is identified as the direct object of the verb 'yaqulu' (he says), and it governs the entire book. Then the name 'al-Tahdhib' is analyzed: it literally means purification from redundancy, and naming the book so is an exaggeration — it is as if the book itself is the act of purification. The commentator notes that he shortened the name from 'Tahdhib al-Kalam fi 'Ilmay al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam' because it is famous by the shorter name. He also notes that he did not firmly attribute the book to al-Sa'd al-Taftazani because the author humbly omitted his own name. The passage ends with al-Attar's gloss on 'al-husna' and 'ziyadah', citing Quran 4:173.

Key Terms
السعادة
الحسنى
الزيادة
التهذيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the name 'al-Tahdhib' used instead of the full title 'Tahdhib al-Kalam fi 'Ilmay al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam'?
A) Because the author preferred brevity
B) Because the shorter name became famous and is sufficient for identification
C) Because the full title is unknown
D) Because the commentator made a mistake

Key Takeaway
The commentator's preface models how a sharh unpacks the meaning of the matn's words and establishes the interpretive framework for the entire work.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
